### Introduction
Post-stroke dysphagia, characterized by the disruption of normal swallowing processes, stands as one of the most prevalent neurological impairments following a cerebrovascular accident. The intricate swallowing mechanism entails coordination between cerebral cortical regions, subcortical structures, and brainstem pathways. Stroke-induced damage to these areas invariably leads to impaired function within this system (Teasell et al., 2005). Among the affected musculature are the laryngeal muscles such as the suprahyoid and thyrohyoid muscles, alongside infrahyoid muscles; all play pivotal roles in orchestrating effective swallowing (Martino et al., 2012). Post-stroke kinematic disruptions and muscle strength deficiencies manifest as reduced oropharyngeal movement, culminating in dysphagia.
Recent therapeutic advancements have explored acupuncture's potential to alleviate post-stroke deficits by modulating cerebral cortical excitability and promoting neurofunctional recovery (Zhao et al., 2015). Acupuncture may enhance neuromuscular excitability hence improving control over swallow-related musculature. Particularly notable is tongue acupuncture—a specialized form of this ancient practice—lauded for its precise targeting of neural circuits integral to swallowing.
Although an expanding body of research has recognized acupuncture’s role in facilitating recovery from post-stroke dysphagia through enhanced muscular coordination and nerve activity modulation (Chen et al., 2020), its procedural specifics remain underexplored relative to optimal application frequencies and long-term efficacy. While prior meta-analyses have concluded tongue acupuncture's superiority over conventional therapy for ameliorating dysphagic symptoms (Yu & Zhang, 2018), a critical variable still warrants rigorous exploration: What is the comparative effectiveness between different frequencies of tongue acupuncture on post-stroke dysphagia?
This study aims to bridge this knowledge gap by investigating how varying session frequencies impact clinical outcomes in individuals with post-stroke dysphagia undergoing tongue acupuncture treatments. The repeated stimulation premise posits that more frequent interventions might engender superior neuromuscular adaptations than less frequent sessions; however, empirical evidence needed for definitive conclusions remains sparse.
Drawing from principles embedded within neuroplasticity—the capacity of neural networks for structural remodeling—there exists a theoretical framework supporting augmented benefits concomitant with higher treatment frequency (Kleim & Jones, 2008). Motor learning paradigms underscore repetition intensity as fundamental to potentiation effects observed amongst recovering stroke patients’ motor functions when subjected repeatedly but varyingly scheduled rehabilitative exercises—corroboration toward extending these findings onto therapeutic paradigms involving fine-tuned applications like tongue acupuncture is necessary.
This inquiry proffers multiple facets relevant both clinically—and theoretically—as comprehension deepens regarding mechanisms underpinning intervention efficacies across varied dosages further delineating nuances essential toward standardized protocols development ensuring optimized patient recoveries. Clinicians stand poised benefitting gleaned insights translating potentially transformative alterations incorporated into individualized rehabilitative strategies tailoring specific needs accentuating ultimately enriched qualitative life improvements amongst afflicted populations enduring debilitating aftermaths attributable strokes’ occurrences nation—and worldwide alike

**Introduction**
Parkinson’s disease (PD) is a neurodegenerative disorder primarily characterized by its motor symptoms, such as bradykinesia, rigidity, and tremor. However, the non-motor symptoms, especially cognitive impairment, are increasingly recognized as critical factors that worsen the prognosis of PD and elevate both caregiver burden and healthcare costs. Cognitive decline in PD ranges from mild cognitive impairment (MCI) to dementia, with approximately 80% of patients ultimately developing dementia during the disease course. Recently, subjective cognitive decline (SCD) has garnered attention as it represents self-reported cognitive deterioration despite the absence of objective impairments in standard neuropsychological testing.
Subjective cognitive decline has been defined within Alzheimer's disease (AD) research circles as an important at-risk state for MCI and a potential prodromal phase for subsequent dementia development. Despite this growing recognition within AD research frameworks, SCD remains relatively underexplored in the context of PD (PD-SCD). Limited empirical studies have examined whether SCD serves similarly as an early marker of impending objective cognitive impairments or even future dementia in individuals with PD.
The sparse research on SCD within Parkinson’s populations underscores several critical gaps that need addressing: there is lack of consensus concerning what constitutes SCD specifically tailored to PD contexts; furthermore no universally accepted assessment tools exist to evaluate this phenomenon reliably. This deficit hinders thorough understanding into whether interventions targeting those who report such declines could potentially stave off more severe later-life deteriorations.
Thus far preliminary investigations suggest that patients experiencing PD-SCD may exhibit underlying neurobiological changes indicative heightened risk transitioning towards MCI or full-blown cases ### Introduction
Hepatocellular carcinoma (HCC), the predominant form of primary liver cancer, continues to climb both in incidence and mortality rates worldwide, presenting formidable challenges for effective management and treatment. Characterized by a multifactorial etiology encompassing chronic liver diseases such as hepatitis B and C infections, alcohol abuse, and nonalcoholic fatty liver disease (NAFLD), HCC's complex pathophysiology often results in late diagnoses and limited therapeutic options. Current standards of care vary from surgical resection to loco-regional therapies like transarterial chemoembolization (TACE) and systemic treatments including tyrosine kinase inhibitors (TKIs) such as sorafenib. Despite these efforts, the prognosis remains dishearteningly poor with a five-year survival rate lingering below 20%.
In recent years, immunotherapy has emerged as a transformative modality for treating various malignancies, including HCC. Immune checkpoint inhibitors (ICIs), exemplified by antibodies targeting programmed cell death protein 1 (PD-1) or its ligand PD-L1 have secured regulatory approval based on their capacity to reinvigorate anti-tumor immunity. However, while remarkable responses have been documented in some subsets of patients, others exhibit primary resistance or develop adaptive resistance over time. The overarching question thus remains: how can we overcome these barriers to optimize clinical outcomes?
Given this backdrop of challenges inherent to immunotherapy for HCC—particularly the conundrum of overcoming resistance—the scientific community has shifted focus towards combination modalities aimed at enhancing therapeutic efficacy. Among the promising candidates are histone deacetylase inhibitors (HDACis). HDACis function via epigenetic modulation; they alter chromatin architecture leading to transcriptional reprogramming which can exert profound effects on tumor biology and immune response regulation.
While recent studies propose that HDACis might sensitize tumors to immunotherapy across various cancers—including melanoma and non-small cell lung cancer—research specifically oriented toward hepatic malignancies is burgeoning yet nascent. The intersectionality between epigenetic modulation through HDAC inhibition and immune checkpoint blockade forms an exciting frontier poised at potentially revolutionizing paradigms in HCC therapy.
However, an equally compelling avenue demands exploration: the potential roles played by metabolic rewiring within this intricate interplay between HDAC inhibition and immune response enhancement in HCC treatment—a question previously understudied relative to traditional oncogenic pathways or immune evasion profiles alone.
Metabolic adaptations constitute hallmarks not only within oncogenesis but extending into responses toward therapeutics whether standalone agents or combinatorial regimens; thus understanding metabolic dynamics could illuminate novel synergistic mechanisms augmenting HDACi utility when conjoined with ICIs against resistant hepatocellular carcinoma phenotypes.

## Introduction
Primary complement system (C) deficiencies, though relatively rare, present a noteworthy clinical implication due to their strong association with heightened susceptibility to infections, autoimmune conditions, and broader immune disorders. The complement system acts as a critical branch of the innate immune response, functioning through its classical, lectin, and alternative pathways to identify and eliminate pathogens efficiently. Among the terminal pathway C deficiencies—comprising C5 through C9 components—the clinical predicament posed by these deficits is underscored by an astronomically elevated risk (1,000- to 10,000-fold) of Neisseria meningitidis infections compared with the general population. Swift diagnosis is warranted for such patients to mitigate additional infection risks and prioritize appropriate prophylactic measures including vaccination.
Prevailing research has extensively mapped genetic mutations underlying various complement component deficiencies; however, limited attention has been accorded to potential modifier genes that might influence disease severity or phenotypic variability in individuals diagnosed with terminal pathway C-deficiencies. Understanding these modifiers could reveal novel therapeutic targets and facilitate personalized management strategies for affected individuals.
A spotlight on Complement Component 7 (C7) deficiency garners particular interest in dissecting genetic nuances beyond primary pathogenic mutations within the C7 gene itself. Characterized predominantly by increased vulnerability to invasive meningococcal infections following perturbations in any singular component of the lytic membrane attack complex (MAC), patients afflicted by this deficiency report conspicuous morbidity profiles worth systematic probing.
In this vein lies our investigative inquiry aimed at elucidating whether non-primary-genetic factors—specifically epigenetic modifications—might assert influence over disease severity in individuals diagnosed with genetically validated C7 deficiency. Epigenetic mechanisms encompass changes such as DNA methylation patterns or histone modifications which do not alter the nucleotide sequence but potentially regulate gene expression dynamics vis-à-vis environmental exposure or intrinsic biological crosstalks.
Existing literature witnesses rare deliberations into ancillary determinants modulating clinical manifestations amongst those burdened with primary complement deficiencies. We propose a shift from silos examining inherent genetic predispositions towards unpacking how addendum layers like epigenetics dovetail into modulating observed pathophysiology.
An illustrative beginning involves revisiting insights furnished by cases akin yet marginally deviant from conventional exemplars propelling our hypothesis formation: Reports evidence instances where siblings sharing identical foundational genotypic disruptions exhibited variable magnitudes of infective episodes or autoimmune co-morbidities insinuating an inter-play meriting deeper excavation beyond mere DNA sequence alterations answering crude 'why' proclivities?

**Introduction**
Tuberculosis (TB), caused by Mycobacterium tuberculosis, persists as a significant global health threat, ranking as one of the top causes of mortality due to infectious diseases. Despite concerted public health efforts for TB control, the disease encompasses approximately a third of the global population either through active or latent infection. One of the major impediments in effectively combating TB is the extended turnaround time and suboptimal sensitivity associated with traditional diagnostic methods such as smear microscopy and culture. The delay from symptom onset to initiation of appropriate treatment facilitates ongoing transmission within communities and cultivates an environment conducive to drug-resistant strains.
In response to these challenges, molecular diagnostics have emerged as potential game-changers in TB diagnosis owing to their enhanced sensitivity and specificities. Nonetheless, such assays often necessitate sophisticated laboratory infrastructure and trained personnel which pose significant limitations for widespread adoption particularly in resource-constrained settings prevalent in high-burden countries.
The concept of utilizing loop-mediated isothermal amplification (LAMP) assay for rapid Mycobacterium spp detection appears promising due to its procedural simplicity enabling visual readouts without needing complex instrumentation. Endorsed by WHO in 2016 for TB diagnosis, LAMP has demonstrated considerable potential; yet there remains a substantial gap concerning its consistent deployment across varied epidemiological landscapes.
Given these perspectives one might ponder on previously unexamined crucial aspects within this realm: "What are healthcare workers' perceptions regarding deploying LAMP-based diagnostics vis-à-vis conventional techniques in battling Mycobacterial infections?"
Understanding healthcare workforce’s insights into diagnostic advancement offers pivotal implications considering their frontline involvement directly impacting patient outcomes through timely intervention strategies especially under constrained environments typical among high prevalence zones like India or Sub-Saharan Africa where access disparities arise markedly amplifying disease burden dynamics multifoldly.

### 1. Introduction
The evolving landscape of cannabis legalization for both medicinal and recreational use has garnered considerable attention from both the public and scientific communities. As the legal framework surrounding cannabis continues to shift, so too does our understanding of its impacts on health, particularly mental health. While much of the research has concentrated on acute adverse events presenting in emergency departments (EDs), a relatively under-explored area is the chronic mental health sequelae associated with long-term cannabis use among different demographic groups.
Recently, a growing body of literature has emerged suggesting that prolonged cannabis consumption may lead to enduring psychiatric conditions such as depression, anxiety disorders, and psychosis. However, these conclusions are fraught with methodological challenges including retrospective study designs, under-reporting biases, and confounding variables related to poly-substance abuse. With numerous jurisdictions reporting varying rates of mental health disorders post-legalization, there is an urgent need for a comprehensive examination into the chronic psychological effects attributable specifically to extended durations of cannabis consumption.
We propose addressing this gap by investigating whether long-term cannabis use differentially impacts various demographic groups in terms of chronic mental health outcomes––such as stress-related disorders or substance-induced psychotic disorders––while accounting for pre-existing psychiatric conditions. Our focus will extend beyond merely characterizing adverse events at a single time point but includes assessing persistent psychiatric symptoms over extended periods.
One primary motivation behind investigating this question stems from accumulating evidence underscoring disparities in how different subpopulations experience mental health consequences related to drug use. Specifically concerning are reports indicating disproportionate burdens among adolescents whose neurodevelopmental trajectories may be particularly sensitive to psychoactive substances like delta-9-tetrahydrocannabinol (THC). Furthermore, emerging findings hint at gender differences whereby women might be more susceptible than men to experiencing anxiety and mood disorders in relation with prolonged marijuana usage despite lower prevalence rates overall for substance abuse within this group.
Another significant avenue worth exploring pertains not only constrained within behavioral domains but also extending towards neurobiological substrates underpinning observed disparities across diverse populations engaging regularly over years’ courses et al.. Title: **Exploring the Synergistic Effects of Histone Deacetylase Inhibitors and Immune Checkpoint Inhibitors in the Treatment of Pheochromocytomas and Paragangliomas**
**Introduction**
Epigenetic mechanisms, including DNA methylation and histone modifications such as acetylation and deacetylation, hold eminent significance in understanding the pathogenesis of numerous malignancies. The regulation of gene expression through these modifications brings forth an undeniable impact on various cellular processes associated with cancer progression. Among these epigenetic modifications, histone acetylation is linked to transcriptional activation, while deacetylation corresponds to transcriptional repression. These processes are primarily governed by two families of enzymes: histone acetyltransferases (HATs) that add acetyl groups to lysine residues on histones, enhancing gene expression; and histone deacetylases (HDACs) that remove these groups, resulting in chromatin condensation and gene repression.
Over recent decades, significant advancements have unveiled compelling evidence that HDAC inhibitors (HDACis) present a novel therapeutic avenue for combating diverse malignancies by inducing cell cycle arrest, promoting apoptosis, stimulating differentiation programs within malignant cells. Given their impact on modulating intricate intracellular pathways mediating response proliferation stress responses based oncological context unraveling efficacious roles therapies against a spectrum hematologic solid cancers showing particular promise myeloma T-cell lymphomas including others thyroid colorectal lung breast pancreatic contexts current research delineates their utilization beyond hitherto explored realms our focus extends unchartered territories lesser-studied indications effective potentially life-saving interventions phenotype transformation neuroendocrine tumors specifically pheochromocytomas paragangliomas.

**Introduction**
Autism spectrum disorder (ASD) is an intricate and multifaceted neurodevelopmental disorder characterized by deficits in social interaction, communication challenges, and repetitive behaviors. The prevalence of ASD has seen a marked increase over the past few decades, with recent estimates suggesting that it affects around 1 in 44 children in the United States alone. Given its broad range and high variability of symptoms, ASD imposes profound psychological and socio-economic burdens on patients, their families, caregivers, and broader societal systems.
Current therapeutic strategies for managing ASD predominantly involve behavioral interventions such as Applied Behavior Analysis (ABA), speech therapy, occupational therapy, as well as pharmacological treatments aimed at ameliorating associated symptoms like irritability or hyperactivity. Despite their widespread adoption and some evidence of efficacy, these therapies often fall short due to several limitations including high costs, limited accessibility particularly in underserved regions or communities with lower socioeconomic status; a wide variability in individual responses; and potential adverse effects of medications.
In recent years there has been growing interest in exploring complementary and alternative medicine (CAM) therapies to bridge these gaps. Among various CAM modalities like nutritional supplements or mindfulness practices currently under investigation for their therapeutic potential against ASD symptoms – acupuncture has garnered attention due to its historical roots going back thousands of years within Traditional Chinese Medicine (TCM), anecdotal success stories propagated through media channels worldwide -yet remains controversial due insufficient robust clinical evidence supporting widespread endorsement within modern biomedical paradigms.
Given this backdrop one pertinent question arises: Can certain sensory-related interventions work synergistically when combined with acupuncture to produce better outcomes than either approach alone? Building upon this query involves delving deeper into understanding personalized intervention strategies where nuanced paths converge offering hope possibly tangible leads which substantiated *Introduction*
Effective communication and information sharing are paramount in the healthcare sector, where the stakes for patient safety and quality of care are significantly high. Past investigations into medical care deficiencies have consistently underscored the importance of fostering an environment conducive to open dialogue among healthcare professionals. Indeed, speaking up about potential risks and procedural lapses—commonly termed "employee voice"—has been extensively studied alongside its counterpoint, "employee silence," which pertains to withholding relevant information that could contribute to improving patient outcomes (Morrison, 2014). Despite a growing body of research dedicated to speaking-up mechanisms in healthcare settings, interventions often yield suboptimal results due primarily to entrenched professional and organizational cultures resistant to open communication (Katz-Navon & Erez, 2005). This highlights an enduring question: why do some employees choose silence over voice even when equipped with potentially critical information?
However, existing literature predominantly emphasizes quantifiable metrics around instances of speaking up or remaining silent without delving deep into the underlying psychological mechanisms influencing these behaviors. Specifically missing is comprehensive attention toward factors like mental health conditions such as anxiety or depression among healthcare staff that potentially mediate their inclination towards voice or silence. Given that roles within healthcare environments are highly demanding both physically and emotionally (National Academies of Sciences, Engineering & Medicine, 2019), it stands to reason that mental well-being may crucially affect whether staff members engage in protective communication behaviors.
Therefore, this paper aims at filling this notable gap by addressing a distinct yet integrative research question: How do mental health conditions such as anxiety and depression influence employee voice and silence in healthcare settings? The nuances surrounding this inquiry promise important insights; understanding how psychological states affect willingness or reluctance to communicate could inform tailored interventions aimed at optimizing employees' mental well-being thus fostering more effective information-sharing dynamics within medical institutions.
The conceptual extension herein draws from interdisciplinary paradigms converging on occupational health psychology as it applies specifically within clinical practice environments. Traditional frameworks defining employee voice often align with behavioral theories positing workplace behavior contingent on perceived support systems (Detert & Edmondson; 2011), whereas organizational psychology extends these constructs further by examining intrinsic motivations shaped through personal experiences antecedent cognitive assessments regarding communicative actions’ utility vis-a-vis personal costs experienced from stressors like anxiety disorders (Kish-Gephart et al., 2009).

**Introduction**
In contemporary nutritional science, there is growing interest in plant-based dietary patterns due to their potential health benefits. Various studies have documented associations between plant-based diets and improved health outcomes such as decreased risk of chronic diseases including cardiovascular disease, diabetes, and certain cancers (Satija et al., 2016; Willett et al., 2019). As interest in these dietary patterns proliferates, so does the need for reliable tools to assess adherence and quality of plant-based diets. This has given rise to a multitude of plant-based diet quality indices aimed at quantifying diet characteristics and correlating them with health metrics.
While existing indices provide meaningful insights into the general population's adherence to healthy eating guidelines, questions remain regarding their applicability across diverse demographic groups. Specifically, little attention has been paid to how these indices perform when applied to different racial and ethnic populations. Acknowledging the unique dietary traditions and food preferences specific to cultural contexts is critical for accurate evaluation (Daniel & Gustafson, 2004). Consequently, it becomes imperative not only to develop comprehensive indices but also to tailor them appropriately in order not just preserve but indeed leverage cultural diversity.
This study aims at bridging this research gap by conducting a nuanced inquiry into how well-established plant-based diet quality indices reflect the dietary habits of various racial-ethnic populations within the United States. Discrepancies could arise due to varied intake patterns influenced by socioeconomic status, access disparities concerning fresh produce or culturally relevant foods (Diez Roux et al., 2001), as well as varying definitions about what constitutes a "healthy" plant-based item among different groups (Patil et al., 2018).
Our objectives can be detailed as follows: 
1) To systematically review existing literature on major racially-ethnically diverse cohorts who adhere predominantly but not exclusively toward consuming vegetarian/vegan fare;
2) Examine whether standardized nutrition labelling settings such though USDA MyPlate diverge correspondingly aligned epidemiologically predictive variables representative;
3) Identify deviations suggestive thereby implicating inaccuracies upon reliability projection measures from broader implementation contexts;

**Title: The Role of Extracellular Vesicle-Derived microRNAs in Modulating Endothelial Cell Function and Atherosclerosis Development**
**Abstract**:
*Extracellular vesicles (EVs) are pivotal mediators of intercellular communication, carrying diverse molecular cargoes, including proteins, lipids, and nucleic acids. Among their cargoes, microRNAs (miRNAs) have emerged as key regulators of gene expression and cellular function. In the context of atherosclerosis—a progressive disease characterized by endothelial dysfunction, inflammation, and plaque formation—EV-derived miRNAs have gained attention for their potential roles in modulating vascular homeostasis and pathology. This study aims to provide a comprehensive overview of how EV-derived miRNAs influence endothelial cell function within the framework of atherosclerotic disease development. By elucidating the mechanisms behind EV-miRNA-mediated endothelial regulation and identifying specific miRNA targets involved in this process, we can better understand their impact on disease progression. Additionally, we discuss advanced methodologies for isolating EVs and profiling miRNA contents from biological samples relevant to cardiovascular research.*
**1\. Introduction**
Atherosclerosis remains one of the leading causes of morbidity and mortality globally due to its contributions to heart attacks and strokes. This chronic inflammatory condition is marked by the accumulation of lipids within arterial walls followed by subsequent immune responses that lead to plaque formation (Libby et al., 2014). Endothelial cells lining blood vessels play a crucial role in maintaining vascular homeostasis; thus, dysfunction at this level serves as an early indicator or even precipitating factor for atherogenesis (Gimbrone & García-Cardeña, 2016).
Recent advances have unveiled extracellular vesicles (EVs)—nanometer-scale membranous particles released into bodily fluids—as significant players not only in cellular communication but also in pathophysiological processes associated with cardiovascular diseases like myocardial infarction or hypertension-induced vascular injury (Jansen et al., 2017). Notably unique among different classes carried by these vesicles are microRNAs (miRNAs), short non-coding RNAs capable fundamentally altering transcriptomic landscapes through post-transcriptional silencing methods.
The constellation composed largely though not exclusively microenvironmental factors implies intricate interplay between high cholesterolemia levels continuous mechanical stress oxidized lipid species all disproportionately affecting responsiveness adaptability tissues positioned towards luminal surfaces influencing overall outcomes ultimately health prognosis.

## Introduction
The field of cardiac electrophysiology has witnessed substantial advancements over recent years, particularly in the optimization of cardiac resynchronization therapy (CRT) for managing heart failure (HF). Conventional biventricular epicardial (BiV) pacing has long been established as a standard in clinical practice to enhance ventricular synchrony and alleviate symptoms among HF patients. However, an innovative approach known as conduction system pacing (CSP) has emerged, garnering attention for its potential merit as a more localized and physiologically harmonized method for CRT delivery. While existing research accentuates the promising nature of CSP overall, limited studies have specifically scrutinized its implications or advantages when applied to atrial fibrillation (AF) cohorts within the broader HF population.
Despite increasing uptake and rising enthusiasm for CSP application in varied clinical circumstances, understanding whether this new modality affects outcomes based on baseline atrial rhythm remains critical but inadequately elucidated. AF is prevalent in about one-third of all HF incidents and is heavily associated with adverse prognosis. The duality presented by these conditions—frequent need of CRT amidst persistently irregular atrial rhythms—poses an intriguing “crosstalk” between synergistic pathology management strategies.
This particular investigation provides a fresh lens through which we assess not merely how CSP fares against conventional modalities but also extends the inquiry into adjunctive therapeutic strategies unique to AF sufferers requiring AV nodal intervention or ablation procedures.
A central postulate warrants exploration: Does concurrent anti-arrhythmic therapy influence left-ventricular ejection fraction improvement from baseline under distinct pacing schemes such as BiV versus His-bundle pursuing rhythms under AVNR-tailored indivisibles?

# Digitalization in Cardiovascular Disease Management: Integration of Data Analytics and Predictive Modeling for Acute Heart Failure
## 1. Introduction
Cardiovascular diseases (CVD) represent one of the leading causes of morbidity and mortality globally, with acute heart failure (AHF) being a significant contributor to adverse health outcomes. AHF is not only a critical stage in the progression of chronic heart disease but also an event that necessitates immediate medical intervention due to its life-threatening nature. In recent years, there has been growing interest in leveraging digital technologies to address healthcare challenges associated with CVD, sparking a potential revolution in diagnostic and therapeutic strategies.
The advent of digitalization offers transformative prospects across various aspects of healthcare by harnessing the power of big data, advanced analytics, and predictive modeling. Emerging technologies such as machine learning algorithms, artificial intelligence (AI), mobile health applications (mHealth), wearable devices, and telemedicine are converging to create an integrated ecosystem that supports continuous monitoring and personalized care.
This academic paper explores the integration of data analytics and predictive modeling within the spectrum of digitalized cardiovascular care to improve management outcomes for patients suffering from AHF. Traditionally managed through established clinical pathways combining pharmacological interventions with lifestyle modification advice, AHF presents unique challenges that benefit from innovative solutions enabled by digital healthcare. This hitherto under-researched domain garners attention due to its potential to augment conventional treatments with technology-driven insights delivering enhanced precision medicine.
To understand how these innovations can be optimally implemented alongside existing therapies requires delving into several subdomains related both directly or indirectly influenced by technological ### Introduction
Metabolic reprogramming, prominently characterized by altered lipid metabolism, has emerged as a fundamental hallmark of cancer. Lipids, one of the primary macromolecules involved in cellular metabolism, play critical roles not only in maintaining the structural integrity of cell membranes but also in serving as vital signaling molecules and energy sources. The multifaceted involvement of lipids in cellular homeostasis underscores their potential impact on various pathological conditions, including tumors. Abnormal lipid metabolism is intricately linked to tumorigenesis and cancer progression by modulating oncogenic signaling pathways. Given this backdrop, the present study aims to delve deeper into an often-overlooked aspect: *the role of specific lipid species—namely fatty acids and phospholipids—in influencing chemotherapy resistance across different tumor types*. 
Chemotherapy remains one of the most conventional treatment modalities for cancer; however, its efficacy is frequently compromised due to the development of resistance by malignant cells. Previous research has predominantly focused on genetic mutations and alterations in drug transporters as primary mechanisms driving chemotherapy resistance. Nonetheless, emerging evidence suggests that metabolic rewiring within tumors markedly influences drug sensitivity and resistance profiles. As part of this metabolic shift, aberrations in fatty acid and phospholipid metabolism have been observed to potentially contribute to a heightened chemoresistant phenotype.
Fatty acids are not merely structural components; they also act as potent bioactivators engaging multiple signaling cascades that foster cell survival under therapeutic stress conditions. Distinct types of fatty acids can exert various effects ranging from promoting oxidative stress resilience to altering membrane fluidity—attributes that grant a survival advantage during chemotherapeutic interventions. Phospholipids constitute another critical class implicated in chemotherapy resistance due to their role in maintaining cellular membrane dynamics which affect drug uptake and efflux processes.
The relationship between abnormal lipid species and chemoresistance necessitates exploration at multiple levels: (1) understanding how specific fatty acids or phospholipids confer adaptive advantages under chemo-stressful conditions; (2) identifying key regulatory enzymes mediating these metabolic shifts; (3) delineating differential responses among diverse tumor subtypes based on inherent lipid profile variances; (4) considering dietary influences that may modify lipid composition within tumors thereby altering treatment outcomes.
Extensive studies have delineated how dysregulated cholesterol or triglyceride biosynthesis contributes broadly towards oncogenic processes such as proliferation or metastasis but remain less detailed about subclass-specific impacts relevant for treatment responsiveness especially concerning unsaturated versus saturated fatty acid derivatives or distinct phosphatidylinositol configurations.
This research targets addressing identified gaps through comprehensive investigations encompassing advanced omics techniques alongside functional assessments aimed at elucidating precise mechanistic pathways implicated when aberrant fat metabolism meets anti-cancer pharmacologics optimally highlighting intervention strategies susceptible towards ameliorating resistive tendencies.

Introduction
Type 2 diabetes (T2D) is an increasingly prevalent chronic metabolic disorder characterized by insulin resistance and a relative deficiency in insulin secretion. The exacerbation of T2D globally has underscored the necessity for developing novel therapeutic strategies aimed at ameliorating hyperglycemia, improving clinical symptoms, and mitigating complications associated with this condition. Traditional pharmacological approaches using agents such as metformin have been the cornerstone for managing T2D; however, their efficacy can be limited by suboptimal glycemic control and adverse effects over long-term use. Consequently, there is heightened interest in integrative medical approaches that combine conventional pharmaceuticals with traditional herbal medicines to achieve more comprehensive management of T2D.
Recent studies have highlighted Jinlida granules, a traditional Chinese medicine (TCM), as a promising adjunctive treatment for T2D. Specifically formulated from various herbal components, Jinlida granules have demonstrated notable hypoglycemic effects in clinical trials when administered alone or concomitantly with metformin. Despite these positive outcomes regarding blood glucose levels, there exists a critical knowledge gap concerning the impact of Jinlida granules on other biomarkers associated with diabetes complications—particularly oxidative stress markers which play a pivotal role in the pathogenesis and progression of diabetic complications.
Oxidative stress is characterized by an imbalance between reactive oxygen species (ROS) production and antioxidant defenses, contributing significantly to beta-cell dysfunction and insulin resistance observed in T2D patients. Elevated levels of oxidative stress markers such as Malondialdehyde (MDA) along with diminished activity of antioxidative enzymes including Superoxide Dismutase (SOD) are commonly documented among individuals suffering from diabetes-related health problems. Thus far, no study has systematically evaluated whether adjunctive therapy incorporating Jinlida granules could exert beneficial alterations on this crucial aspect beyond its hypoglycemic capabilities.
Furthermore, understanding how complementary therapies like Jinlida influence systemic biochemical pathways may afford deeper insights into holistic therapeutic strategies that address both symptomatic relief and molecular stability inherent within chronic diseases like T2D.
Our current research aims to bridge this knowledge void by investigating "The Impact of Jinlida Granules Combined With Metformin on Oxidative Stress Markers in Patients With Type 2 Diabetes: A Randomized Controlled Trial." This study will primarily focus on assessing changes induced upon key oxidative stress parameters amongst patients receiving dual therapy compared against those treated solely via metformin monotherapy over twelve weeks duration period defined akin previous trials indicating efficacy through symptomological metrics evaluation standpoint alone not fully encompassing dynamics involved biochemically under context modulated intervention scales overlapping studied subsets representative larger implications evaluation strata validation encompassing.
This investigation targets four primary objectives:
1) To measure baseline oxidative stress markers MDA levels alongside SOD activities across cohort groups prior initiating scheduled interventions randomized cohort structure thereby facilitating initial standardized comparability data collections warranted statistical dilations compensations.

Title: The Role of Extracellular Vesicles in β-cell Function and Survival under Oxidative Stress Conditions
Abstract: Diabetes mellitus (DM) is a progressive metabolic disorder characterized by chronic hyperglycemia due to insulin deficiency or dysfunction. Recent advancements have pointed toward extracellular vesicles (EVs) as pivotal players in cellular communication, with significant potential to serve as both biomarkers and therapeutic tools. Within this context, the role of EVs in preserving β-cell function and enhancing cell survival under conditions of oxidative stress is an area deserving intense investigation. Oxidative stress is a crucial factor contributing to β-cell apoptosis and impaired insulin secretion, thus exacerbating DM pathology. In this review, we focus on the role of EVs in mediating protective signals that enhance β-cell resilience against oxidative insults, exploring the underlying mechanisms and potential clinical applications. Understanding how EVs foster β-cell survival under oxidative stress may pave the way for novel diagnostic biomarkers and innovative therapeutic strategies aimed at preserving pancreatic islet health.
1. Introduction
Diabetes mellitus (DM) continues to be a major global health challenge due to its increasing prevalence, complex pathophysiology, and associated high mortality rates. Traditional therapeutic interventions primarily focus on mitigating hyperglycemia through either enhancing insulin secretion or improving peripheral insulin sensitivity; however, these approaches often fail owing both to their limited efficacy over time and their inability to address underlying pathogenic mechanisms such as oxidative stress.
Oxidative stress refers to an imbalance between reactive oxygen species (ROS) production and antioxidant defense systems within cells—a scenario detrimental particularly for pancreatic β-cells which are inherently susceptible due largely but not exclusively due limited intrinsic antioxidant defenses intrinsicated low inherent expression levels key enzymatic activities including superoxide dismutase catalases glutathione peroxidase whereas unsuccessful addressing induced further contribute sequentially onto spiraling vicious cycle compromises overall tissue viability integrity functionality directly indirectly leading obliterating exasperated progressing inexorably complete futile burnout ultimate eventual demise altogether closely linked directly integral stressed events backdrop continually drives strongly aggregates insurmountable dysregulation systemic impairments metabolic outcomes particularly typified cardinal principal hallmark referenced contributory defined fundamentally multifactorial polygenetic phenotypic implicates extensively predominately propels precipitates sustaining worsening perpetuating deleterious vicious cumulative attributable encompassing seriously necessitating more robust effective precisely targeted comprehensive non-conventional biomedical translational modalities.

### Introduction
Heart failure (HF) constitutes a significant global health burden, affecting over 64 million individuals worldwide and leading to considerable morbidity, mortality, and healthcare costs. Due to its intricate pathophysiology and heterogeneous nature, HF management necessitates multifaceted approaches encompassing lifestyle changes, pharmacological interventions, device therapies, and sometimes surgical procedures. Among recent pharmacological advancements in HF management are sodium-glucose cotransporter-2 inhibitors (SGLT-2is), originally developed as antidiabetic agents but now recognized for their cardiovascular benefits.
SGLT-2 inhibitors modulate glucose reabsorption in the renal proximal tubules by selectively inhibiting the SGLT-2 protein. In doing so, these agents not only improve glycemic control but also exert a series of beneficial pleiotropic effects such as osmotic diuresis and natriuresis which can contribute to reducing cardiac preload and afterload. Furthermore, they have been shown to influence various neurohormonal pathways implicated in HF pathogenesis favorably. The landmark trials—DAPA-HF (Dapagliflozin And Prevention of Adverse-outcomes in Heart Failure) for example—have demonstrated the efficacy of SGLT-2is in reducing both hospitalizations due to heart failure (HHF) and cardiovascular death across different subpopulations of patients with HF.
While substantial evidence highlights the general effectiveness of SGLT-2 inhibitors across diverse populations comprising both men and women with varying risk profiles akin to those seen among people suffering from HF with reduced ejection fraction (HFrEF), uncertainties persist regarding sex-specific responses to this class of medication. The available data suggest that biological differences related primarily—but incompletely—to hormonal influences might underpin distinctive outcomes between sexes when treated with identical therapeutic regimens.
In light of the growing recognition that sex-based analyses are vital for personalized medicine—and acknowledging preliminary observations alluding to potential disparities—the necessity arises for more nuanced interrogations addressing gender dissimilarities concerning specific facets within broader health contexts.
 
The previously conducted meta-analysis indicated variances concerning primary composite outcomes contingent on patient gender amongst diabetic cohorts treated using SGLT  - inhibition techniques; similar trends could manifest themselves similarly within prevailing heart-failure cases examined under randomized control trials featuring said therapeutic modalities specifically targeting measured cardiovascular parameters — indeed advancing our comprehension enables better tailoring sleuth avenues improving primary endpoints irrespective internally linked mechanisms distinctive biological synopsis varying anatomically contextual snapshots undertaken thereby adjustments ultimately conceived guiding protocol formulations ensuing favorable prognostication insight paradigms.
